#PROJECT
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Metabolic Profiling of Date Palm Fruits
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	The goal of this study was to investigate metabotypes of date palm fruits
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	through global, non-targeted metabolomics of assorted date fruits varieties from
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	different countries of origin.
PR:INSTITUTE                     	Weill Cornell Medicine Qatar
PR:DEPARTMENT                    	Bioinformatics Core
PR:LABORATORY                    	Suhre Lab

PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	of Qatar Foundation under the National Priorities Research Program â€“

#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	Metabolic Profiling of Date Palm Fruits (part II)
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	In this study, two independent large cohorts of mature dates exhibiting
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	substantial diversity in origin, varieties and fruit processing conditions were
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	measured by metabolomics techniques in order to identify major determinants of
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	the fruit metabotype. Additional samples reflecting different stages of date
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	fruit ripening process has been included for 10 different fruit varieties. This
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	study includes updated date photographs and combined results data (GCMS/LCMS)
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	and technical validation data, see downloadable files section to access this
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	information.
ST:INSTITUTE                     	Weill Cornell Medicine in Qatar
ST:DEPARTMENT                    	Bioinformatics Core
ST:LABORATORY                    	Suhre Lab
ST:LAST_NAME                     	Suhre
ST:FIRST_NAME                    	Karsten
ST:ADDRESS                       	Education City
ST:EMAIL                         	nis2034@qatar-med.cornell.edu
ST:PHONE                         	+97433888408

#COLLECTION
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	In the present study, 123 unique date varieties (Phoenix dactylifera) from 14
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	countries were collected in two separate occasions: A first collection took part
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	in 2012 (DS1) and the second one in 2013 (DS2). The term variety is used here to
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	describe a distinct phenotypic class of dates and if the same variety was
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	collected from different countries, a different sample ID was assigned to each
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	collected sample per country. Overall, dates from the first sample collection
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	were mostly from the Gulf region obtained in a fairly dried condition from shops
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	and festivals whilst the second sample collection was dominated by North African
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	dates obtained mostly fresh from the palm trees. For the second collection of
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	dates, field work permissions were obtained verbally from owners of visited
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	oases. The marketed versus fresh nature of dates between the two sample
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	collections implies varying post-harvest conditions. All collected dates with
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	homogenous brown color were further dried by exposing them to open air for two
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	weeks before further processing. With the second sample collection, while
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	harvesting ripened fruits from the palm trees, immature fruits still undergoing
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	ripening activity and occasionally late green Kimri fruits from the pre-ripening
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	stage were collected when available. In total, 37 immature date fruits,
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	corresponding to 10 date samples, were collected. With each of the 10 samples,
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	the immature fruits were ranked by their extent of ripening based on visual
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	assessment of color change and skin wrinkling. Each fruit was given an ID based
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	on a combination of the sample number and a letter reflecting the fruit rank
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	within the sample. In general, dates were considered mature if the low moisture
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	prevented any further change in their appearance. Notably, maturity is attained
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	naturally with the dry class of dates but often artificially with the soft class
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	of dates owing to intrinsically higher moisture levels.
CO:SAMPLE_TYPE                   	Date palm fruit
CO:COLLECTION_LOCATION           	Differnt locations specified in the
CO:COLLECTION_DURATION           	2012 - 2013
CO:STORAGE_CONDITIONS            	-80C
#TREATMENT
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	The aim of this study was to determine metabolic phenotype of the date palm
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	fruits without any treatment at the baseline.
#SAMPLEPREP
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Sample pre-processing for DS1: 50 mg of the peel and flesh of the date fruits
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	were flash frozen in liquid nitrogen and extracted as previously described
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	(PMID:21699588). Sample pre-processing for DS2 The beads were added to the
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	pre-weighed frozen samples together with water (8 ÂµL of per mg of sample) for
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	homogenisation. The samples were continuously stirred on the GenoGrinder (Glen
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Mills GenoGrinder 2000, Germany) at 1000 strokes per minute for five minutes, to
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	ensure complete homogenization. 100 ÂµL of aliquot from each sample was
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	transferred to the plates. The samples were loaded on three plates. To each
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	sample, 450 ÂµL of extraction solvent (MeOH with 10 ÂµL /ml chlorophenylalanine,
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	2.5 ÂµL /ml 2-fluorophenylglycine, 25 Âµg/ml d-6 cholestrol and 25 ÂµL /ml
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	tridecanoic acid) was added. The samples were then shaken on the GenoGrinder
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	(GenoGrinder, Spex, USA) at 675 strokes per min for two minutes and centrifuged
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	at 2000 rpm for 5 minutes on a Beckman centrifuge (Beckman GS-6R Centrifuge,
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	USA) at 40C. The extracted samples were divided into equal parts for
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	metabolomics analysis on the Gas Chromatography Mass Spectrometry (GC/MS) and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	the Orbitrap Elite accurate Liquid Chromatography Mass Spectrometry2 (LC-MS-MS)
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	platforms. Four sets of samples were prepared by the Hamilton robot (Hamilton
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Star, Germany) by transferring 110 ÂµL aliquots from each well to three PCR
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	plates, each for LC positive, LC negative, replicate set and one to 250 ÂµL auto
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	sampler vial inserts for GC. All samples were dried for 120 minutes by using a
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Zymark Turbovap 96 (Zymark Turbovap, USA) followed by overnight incubation in a
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	drybox to ensure optimal dryness of the sample. Sample processing DS1 and DS2
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Metabolite measurements with Ultrahigh Performance Liquid Chromatography/Mass
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Spectroscopy (UPLC/MS/MS): The UPLC/MS/MS analysis was based on the Waters
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	ACUITY ultra performance liquid chromatography (Waters Corporation, USA) and the
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	ThermoFischer Scientific Orbitrap Elite high-resolution accurate mass
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	spectrometer (Thermo Fischer Scientific Inc., USA) equipped with a heated
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	electrospray ionization (HESI) source and an Orbitrap mass analyzer. The dried
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	sample extracts for the LC positive and LC negative mode were reconstituted in
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	acidic and basic LC- compatible solvents. Two independent injections were
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	performed on each sample using separate dedicated columns for optimized acidic
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	positive ions and the other for optimized basic negative ions. The acidic
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	samples were reconstituted by gradient elution of water and methanol containing
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	0.1 % formic acid whereas; the basic samples were reconstituted by gradient
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	elution of water and methanol containing 6.5mM ammonium bicarbonate (PMID:
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	19624122). The mass spectra analysis alternated between MS and data dependent
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	MS2 scans using dynamic exclusion. Metabolite measurements with GC/MS: The
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	samples assigned for the GC/MS analysis were further dried under vacuum
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	desiccation for an entire day and derivatized under dried nitrogen using
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	bistrimethyl-silyl-trifluoroacetamide (BSTFA). The GS/MS analysis was based on a
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Thermo FinniganTM TRACETM DSQTM (ThermoFinnigan, USA) fast-scanning single
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	â€“quadrupole mass spectrophotometer using electron impact ionization source.
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	The GC column was 5% phenyl and the temperature ramp range was from 40 to 3000 C
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	in a time span of 16 minutes.
#CHROMATOGRAPHY
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	The 5% diphenyl/ 95% dimethyl polysiloxane GC column and the temperature ramp
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	was from 40Â° to 300Â° C in a 16 minute period. Samples were analyzed on a
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	Thermo-Finnigan Trace DSQ fast-scanning single-quadrupole mass spectrometer
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	using electron impact ionization. The instrument was tuned and calibrated for
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	mass resolution and mass accuracy on a daily basis.
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_TYPE        	GC/MS
CH:INSTRUMENT_NAME            	Thermo-Finnigan Trace DSQ fast-scanning single-quadrupole mass spectrometer
CH:COLUMN_NAME                	5% diphenyl/ 95% dimethyl polysiloxane GC column
